Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Employee: Judy Kobus
Report Date: 2020-11-17
Doctor: Christie Pilossof
Nurse: Lebo Cindi
Clinical Recommendations: Clinically you examine well with normal vitals. There were good blood pressure readings noted. Regular self breast examinations are important to detect any irregularities early. If any concerns, to consult your GP.
Men's Health Recommendations: 
Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: We use body mass index (BMI) and waist to height ratio (WHtR) to assess the distribution of excess body fat. People who carry more weight around their mid section, are at higher risk for heart disease, type 2 diabetes and cancer. Your BMI and your waist circumference are high. Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Deficient vitamin D level: supplement with vitamin D and recheck in 4 to 6 months aiming for a level between 50 to 80 ng/ml. Vitamin D is not only important for your bones but also your mood and cognitive health. It is also has anti-inflammatory and anti-cancer properties.
Comment Key: ClinicalExamComment
Comment Value: None
Special Investigation Notes: Low DHEA

Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.

Overview Notes: Deficient vitamin D
Slightly increased total and LDL cholesterol with low HDL
Increased hsCRP
Increased BMI and waist circumference
Slightly raised uric acid
Comment Key: ClinicalExamNote

Nurse: Lebo Cindi

Men's Health Recommendations: 
Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Overview Notes: We use body mass index (BMI) and waist to height ratio (WHtR) to assess the distribution of excess body fat. People who carry more weight around their mid section, are at higher risk for heart disease, type 2 diabetes and cancer. Your BMI and your waist circumference are high. Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Deficient vitamin D level: supplement with vitamin D and recheck in 4 to 6 months aiming for a level between 50 to 80 ng/ml. Vitamin D is not only important for your bones but also your mood and cognitive health. It is also has anti-inflammatory and anti-cancer properties.
Comment Key: ClinicalExamRecommendation
Comment Value: None
Special Investigation Notes: Low DHEA

Doctor: Christie Pilossof
Nurse: Lebo Cindi
Clinical Recommendations: 
Men's Health Recommendations: 
Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Raised hsCRP: suggests increased levels of inflammation in the body which puts you at higher risk for heart disease and other chronic diseases. Things to consider to lower inflammation include a healthy mediterranean style diet, exercise, stress reduction, omega 3's and curcumin.
Comment Key: LabTestNote
Comment Value: Deficient vitamin D, Raised uric acid, increased cholesterol, increased hsCRP
Special Investigation Notes: Low DHEA

Men's Health Recommendations: 
Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Overview Notes: We use body mass index (BMI) and waist to height ratio (WHtR) to assess the distribution of excess body fat. People who carry more weight around their mid section, are at higher risk for heart disease, type 2 diabetes and cancer. Your BMI and your waist circumference are high. Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Overview Notes: Deficient vitamin D level: supplement with vitamin D and recheck in 4 to 6 months aiming for a level between 50 to 80 ng/ml. Vitamin D is not only important for your bones but also your mood and cognitive health. It is also has anti-inflammatory and anti-cancer properties.
Comment Key: LabTestRecommendation
Comment Value: None
Special Investigation Notes: Low DHEA

Men's Health Recommendations: 
Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Deficient vitamin D level: supplement with vitamin D and recheck in 4 to 6 months aiming for a level between 50 to 80 ng/ml. Vitamin D is not only important for your bones but also your mood and cognitive health. It is also has anti-inflammatory and anti-cancer properties.
Comment Key: LifestyleRecommendation
Comment Value: None
Special Investigation Notes: Low DHEA

Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Deficient vitamin D level: supplement with vitamin D and recheck in 4 to 6 months aiming for a level between 50 to 80 ng/ml. Vitamin D is not only important for your bones but also your mood and cognitive health. It is also has anti-inflammatory and anti-cancer properties.
Comment Key: MensHealthRecommendation
Comment Value: None
Special Investigation Notes: Low DHEA

Nurse: Lebo Cindi
Clinical Recommendations: Clinically you examine well with normal vitals. There were good blood pressure readings noted. Regular self breast examinations are important to detect any irregularities early. If any concerns, to consult your GP.
Men's Health Recommendations: 
Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: We use body mass index (BMI) and waist to height ratio (WHtR) to assess the distribution of excess body fat. People who carry more weight around their mid section, are at higher risk for heart disease, type 2 diabetes and cancer. Your BMI and your waist circumference are high. Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.

Doctor: Christie Pilossof
Nurse: Lebo Cindi
Clinical Recommendations: Clinically you examine well with normal vitals. There were good blood pressure readings noted. Regular self breast examinations are important to detect any irregularities early. If any concerns, to consult your GP.
Men's Health Recommendations: 
Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Increased cholesterol and low HDL: try to manage with lifestyle alone. Eat a healthy diet, increase your exercise, lose weight, decrease your alcohol consumption and manage your stress. Supplement with 2g per day of omega 3.

Nurse: Lebo Cindi
Clinical Recommendations: 
Men's Health Recommendations: 
Women's Health Recommendations: I am glad to hear that you are up-to-date with your screening (Mammogram/ Pap smear). Overview Notes: We use body mass index (BMI) and waist to height ratio (WHtR) to assess the distribution of excess body fat. Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Raised hsCRP: suggests increased levels of inflammation in the body which puts you at higher risk for heart disease and other chronic diseases. Things to consider to lower inflammation include a healthy mediterranean style diet, exercise, stress reduction, omega 3's and curcumin.

Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: We use body mass index (BMI) and waist to height ratio (WHtR) to assess the distribution of excess body fat. People who carry more weight around their mid section, are at higher risk for heart disease, type 2 diabetes and cancer. Your BMI and your waist circumference are high. Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.
Comment Key: ReportRecommendation
Comment Value: None
Special Investigation Notes: Low DHEA

Overview Notes: We use body mass index (BMI) and waist to height ratio (WHtR) to assess the distribution of excess body fat. People who carry more weight around their mid section, are at higher risk for heart disease, type 2 diabetes and cancer. Your BMI and your waist circumference are high. Try to reduce your BMI to 25 and waist circumference to 80 cm.

Report Date: 2020-11-17
Doctor: Christie Pilossof
Nurse: Lebo Cindi

Men's Health Recommendations:

Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: We use body mass index (BMI) and waist to height ratio (WHtR) to assess the distribution of excess body fat. Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Deficient vitamin D level: supplement with vitamin D and recheck in 4 to 6 months aiming for a level between 50 to 80 ng/ml. Vitamin D is not only important for your bones but also your mood and cognitive health. It is also has anti-inflammatory and anti-cancer properties.
Comment Key: SymptomScreeningRecommendation
Comment Value: None
Special Investigation Notes: Low DHEA

Regular review helps to detect any abnormalities early & improves management outcomes. Another screening scan that to be done is a Bone Density. This can be done through any radiology department.
Overview Notes: Increased cholesterol and low HDL: try to manage with lifestyle alone. Eat a healthy diet, increase your exercise, lose weight, decrease your alcohol consumption and manage your stress. Supplement with 2g per day of omega 3.
